									"blurb" : "When the first three D-backs batters went deep in Philadelphia on Monday night, it was a sign of things to come.\nArizona and Philadelphia combined to hit 13 home runs at Citizens Bank Park, setting a new Major League record by both teams in a game. The D-backs won, 13-8.",
									"body" : "<p>When the first three D-backs batters went deep in Philadelphia on Monday night, it was a sign of things to come.\n\nArizona and Philadelphia combined to hit 13 home runs at Citizens Bank Park, setting a new Major League record by both teams in a game. The [D-backs won, 13-8](https://www.mlb.com/news/d-backs-hit-3-straight-home-runs-to-start-game \"undefined\").</p><p><forge-entity title=\"Jarrod Dyson\" slug=\"jarrod-dyson-502481\" code=\"player\">Jarrod Dyson</forge-entity>, <forge-entity title=\"Ketel Marte\" slug=\"ketel-marte-606466\" code=\"player\">Ketel Marte</forge-entity> and <forge-entity title=\"David Peralta\" slug=\"david-peralta-444482\" code=\"player\">David Peralta</forge-entity>, the first three D-backs batters of the night, got Arizona going with back-to-back-to-back blasts on its way to a club-record eight long balls. <forge-entity title=\"Eduardo Escobar\" slug=\"eduardo-escobar-500871\" code=\"player\">Eduardo Escobar</forge-entity> and <forge-entity title=\"Ildemaro Vargas\" slug=\"ildemaro-vargas-545121\" code=\"player\">Ildemaro Vargas</forge-entity> each slugged two in the game, and <forge-entity title=\"Alex Avila\" slug=\"alex-avila-488671\" code=\"player\">Alex Avila</forge-entity> hit one as well.\n\n\u201cIt was just good to get it going,\u201d Dyson said. \u201cLeading off with a homer set the tone and guys came behind me and did the same thing. We\u2019ve been swinging some good bats lately and we\u2019re just trying to continue it. We\u2019re just trying to get a good pitch to hit. That\u2019s the goal, that\u2019s the gameplan when we get in the box. We know that\u2019s a great ballclub over there, and we\u2019re just trying to come out and give our pitcher a little cushion.\u201d\n\n<forge-entity title=\"Scott Kingery\" slug=\"scott-kingery-664068\" code=\"player\">Scott Kingery</forge-entity> hit two of five by the Phillies, who also got one each from <forge-entity title=\"Jean Segura\" slug=\"jean-segura-516416\" code=\"player\">Jean Segura</forge-entity>, <forge-entity title=\"Rhys Hoskins\" slug=\"rhys-hoskins-656555\" code=\"player\">Rhys Hoskins</forge-entity> and <forge-entity title=\"Jay Bruce\" slug=\"jay-bruce-457803\" code=\"player\">Jay Bruce</forge-entity>. It was Hoskins' shot in the ninth that tied the record and Bruce, two batters later, who hit the record-breaker.</p><p>\"I didn\u2019t know that \\[it was a record\\] until I got back in here, but for some reason the ball was just absolutely flying,\" Kingery said. \"It felt like every ball that went in the air was a home run. I\u2019m not sure if that had to do with the weather, the humidity, I don\u2019t know. It was just crazy out there.\"\n\n\"I think tonight was a good indication of how the ball travels here in the middle of the summer,\" Phillies manager Gabe Kapler said.\n\nPhiladelphia starter Jerad Eickhoff took the brunt of Arizona's output, giving up five home runs in three-plus innings. He was lifted in the fourth after issuing a leadoff walk followed by Escobar's first homer of the game, then another walk preceding Avila's blast.\n\n\"I couldn\u2019t adjust,\" Eickhoff said. \"I couldn't adjust to everything. I\u2019d do a thing here, wouldn\u2019t adjust, it didn\u2019t work out, make an adjustment here, it didn\u2019t work. It was just kind of one of those nights. Every mistake I made they were able to put a pretty good swing on it. They were able to do that throughout the night. The most frustrating thing is just not keeping us in the game.\"\n\nThe new record could have been 14, but a drive by Philadelphia's <forge-entity title=\"Nick Williams\" slug=\"nick-williams-608384\" code=\"player\">Nick Williams</forge-entity> in the eighth inning that was originally ruled a home run was changed to a double following review.</p><p>The previous Major League record of 12 was held by the Tigers and White Sox -- who did it against each other twice, on May 28, 1995, at Tiger Stadium, and again on July 2, 2002, at Guaranteed Rate Field. The National League record had been 11, accomplished four times. The last instance was May 17, 1979, by the Cubs and Phillies in 10 innings at Wrigley Field. The only nine-inning game of the four in the NL was on June 11, 1967, between the Cubs and Mets in Chicago.\n\n\u201cYou can\u2019t really explain it,\u201d D-backs manager Torey Lovullo said of the new record. \u201cIt was just a bunch of really good hitters getting after it and not letting up on the gas pedal.\u201d</p>",

									"blurb" : "MIAMI -- Needless to say Cardinals right-hander Michael Wacha didn't go through his typical routine prior to Monday's start against the Marlins.\nThanks to a 4 a.m. ET arrival Monday following a late game in Chicago on Sunday night, Wacha didn't fall asleep until about 5 a.m. His alarm clock",
									"body" : "<p>MIAMI -- Needless to say Cardinals right-hander [Michael Wacha](https://www.mlb.com/player/michael-wacha-608379 \"undefined\") didn't go through his typical routine prior to Monday's start against the Marlins.\n\nThanks to a 4 a.m. ET arrival Monday following a late game in Chicago on Sunday night, Wacha didn't fall asleep until about 5 a.m. His alarm clock woke him up at 2 p.m. so that he could eat, and he slept for another two hours before the team bus left a little after 4 p.m. for Marlins Park.\n\n\"I could've slept longer, easily, but I knew it was time to go to work,\" Wacha said.\n\nAnd that Wacha did, as he outdueled former St. Louis prospect Sandy Alcantara in a 4-1 win over the Marlins in the series opener.\n\n\u2022 [Box score](https://www.mlb.com/gameday/567391/final/box \"undefined\")\n\nWacha pitched six scoreless innings in a triumphant return to the rotation, with his night concluding on his 75th pitch -- an 86.8 mph changeup to strike out Starlin Castro with two men on base in a four-run game.\n\nThough Wacha's average fastball velocity was down (91.9 mph, compared to 92.6 mph) from this season per Statcast, he induced 10 groundouts, including three double plays. Monday marked his first scoreless start of six innings or more since June 3, 2018, against the Pirates.</p><p>  \n\n\"Pitched the ball down in the zone, got in on some guys, made them chase some balls out and away from there,\" said Wacha, who walked two and struck out four. \"Just got some weak contact and let the defense play. That's how I've been successful in the past. Good to get back to it.\"\n\n  \n\nAnother pivotal moment took place in the third, as the first two batters reached on a single and a walk. With Alcantara at the plate, Wacha picked off the lead runner after a replay review overturned the original call. Alcantara was unable to execute a sacrifice bunt and Austin Dean grounded out to end the frame.</p><p>  \n\n  \n\n  \n\n  \n\nAccording to Cardinals manager Mike Shildt, the daylight play was executed \"on the fly\" with Wacha and shortstop Yairo Munoz -- who started in place of Paul DeJong -- being on the same page.\n\n  \n\n  \n\n\"I just checked the field conditions when I tried to dive for a ball toward center field \\[earlier and\\] I slipped a little bit, so I knew it was going to be hard for him to get back to the base,\" Munoz said through an interpreter. \"That's when I decided to give it a try. Of course, Wacha made an excellent throw. All the credit to him.\"</p><p>Wacha, who spent a little over a week on the injured list in late April with left knee patellar tendinitis, wasn't the same upon his return. Over five starts, he compiled a 6.39 ERA that lost him a rotation spot by May 22. Monday was his first quality start since April 17 -- his last appearance before the IL stint.\n\nTwenty-two-year-old prospect Genesis Cabrera made two turns through the rotation in Wacha's stead, before an encouraging 2 1/3-inning scoreless relief outing last Tuesday against the Reds got Wacha the nod Monday.\n\n\u201cHe looked like Wacha,\" Shildt said. \"He kind of established himself. The last outing we saw in relief was very favorable. It gave us rightful confidence that he would get back out there, and he was tremendous tonight, really threw the ball well. There was life to his ball. The changeup worked, and just excellent job by Michael all around.\u201d</p><p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\"><p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Via Statcast, a look at Michael Wacha&#39;s 75 pitches in Monday&#39;s 4-1 win over the Marlins. <a href=\"https://t.co/5F221alqil\">pic.twitter.com/5F221alqil</a></p>&mdash; Christina De Nicola (@CDeNicola13) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/CDeNicola13/status/1138302628063043584?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">June 11, 2019</a></blockquote>\n<script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n</p><p>  \n\nWith Adam Wainwright [landing on the IL](https://www.mlb.com/cardinals/news/adam-wainwright-to-injured-list-with-hamstring-injury \"undefined\"), and the starters struggling over the weekend in a series sweep to Chicago, Wacha's strong effort couldn't have come at a better time.\n\nAsked whether Wacha's outing meant that he would start again Saturday against the Mets, Shildt said, \"I think that's fair to say.\"\n\n\"It was important. It was important to solidify ... Michael to get back in that spot,\" Shildt said. \"Create an opportunity for the rotation, but also it was important for our bullpen. We just got through three games in a row with not getting through the fifth inning. So it was important for that, and for Michael to reestablish and get back to being an anchor in our starting rotation.\u201d</p>",

If they beat us, they beat us. But they better beat us because they beat us, not because we weren\u2019t prepared for it or we didn\u2019t compete.\n\n\u2022 [Box score](https://www.mlb.com/gameday/rangers-vs-red-sox/2019/06/10/565057#game_state=final,game_tab=box,game=565057 \"undefined\")\n\n\u201cOur guys, I think that\u2019s easy to say because we don\u2019t quit.\u201d\n\nNo, the Rangers did not quit. Just when it looked like another strong outing by <forge-entity title=\"Mike Minor\" slug=\"mike-minor-501985\" code=\"player\">Mike Minor</forge-entity> (8 innings, 4 hits, 2 runs, 6 strikeouts) would fall short without run support (5 runs in last 4 starts) the Rangers put together a ninth-inning rally and extra-innings battle to win, 4-3 in 11 innings.\n\nThe comeback marked the Rangers\u2019 first win of the season when trailing after eight innings (1-25). They snapped a seven-game losing streak at Fenway Park dating back to July 5, 2016. The Rangers also broke a skid of four straight series-opening losses and improved to 6-16 in that category.\n\n\u201cThe fact that we keep just pressuring teams in the late innings -- regardless of how the beginning or the first seven innings or the first six innings went -- we just have really good character in that ballclub,\u201d Woodward said. \u201cI\u2019m proud of our guys because they just keep on fighting.\u201d</p><p>  \n\n  \n\nMinor put the Rangers in position for a comeback after holding the Red Sox scoreless in his final seven innings pitched. While Minor was critical of all his pitches except for his slider -- \u201cI don\u2019t know how I got through it really. It wasn\u2019t a good night for me,\u201d he said -- his ERA dropped to 2.10 over his last nine starts.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m proud of Mike,\u201d Woodward said. \u201cHe\u2019s kind of trying to prove to the world that he\u2019s an elite pitcher.\u201d\n\nTrailing 2-1 entering the ninth after <forge-entity title=\"Chris Sale\" slug=\"chris-sale-519242\" code=\"player\">Chris Sale</forge-entity>'s 10-strikeout, 7-inning outing, <forge-entity title=\"Danny Santana\" slug=\"danny-santana-542454\" code=\"player\">Danny Santana</forge-entity> singled off Boston reliever <forge-entity title=\"Matt Barnes\" slug=\"matt-barnes-598264\" code=\"player\">Matt Barnes</forge-entity> and <forge-entity title=\"Elvis Andrus\" slug=\"elvis-andrus-462101\" code=\"player\">Elvis Andrus</forge-entity> followed with a double that put runners on second and third with one out. <forge-entity title=\"Nomar Mazara\" slug=\"nomar-mazara-608577\" code=\"player\">Nomar Mazara</forge-entity> singled to left to drive in the go-ahead run.</p><p><forge-entity title=\"Shawn Kelley\" slug=\"shawn-kelley-518875\" code=\"player\">Shawn Kelley</forge-entity>, who had been scoreless in 13 of his previous 16 games, took the mound in the bottom of the frame to close out the victory. The Red Sox, though, had other plans and tied the game 2-2 off a Brock Holt RBI single to score pinch-runner <forge-entity title=\"Michael Chavis\" slug=\"michael-chavis-656308\" code=\"player\">Michael Chavis</forge-entity> and force extra innings.\n\nThe Rangers called upon <forge-entity title=\"Jesse Chavez\" slug=\"jesse-chavez-445926\" code=\"player\">Jesse Chavez</forge-entity> and his 21 2/3-innings scoreless streak in the 10th. He walked the bases loaded with two outs but got <forge-entity title=\"Xander Bogaerts\" slug=\"xander-bogaerts-593428\" code=\"player\">Xander Bogaerts</forge-entity> to line out to center to end the threat.\n\nJust like in the ninth, Santana got on base to start the 11th inning with a double off <forge-entity title=\"Ryan Brasier\" slug=\"ryan-brasier-518489\" code=\"player\">Ryan Brasier</forge-entity>. And just like in the ninth, Andrus followed with a single in the next at-bat. This time, Andrus\u2019 ground ball to center was enough to bring Santana around for what proved to be the winning run.</p><p>  \n\nSantana finished the night 4-for-5 with two doubles, two runs scored and an RBI.\n\n\u201c\\[This is\\] a very good win for us as we are competing for first place,\u201d Santana said in Spanish.\n\nThe Rangers' win increased their lead over both the Red Sox and Indians to two games in the American League Wildcard standings. PETERSBURG -- When Kevin Kiermaier is clicking both offensively and defensively, it\u2019s tough to argue that he shouldn\u2019t be mentioned among the best center fielders in the American League.\nIn the seventh inning of the Rays\u2019 6-2 win over the Athletics at Tropicana Field, Kiermaier showed off his Platinum",
									"body" : "<p>ST. PETERSBURG -- When Kevin Kiermaier is clicking both offensively and defensively, it\u2019s tough to argue that he shouldn\u2019t be mentioned among the best center fielders in the American League.\n\nIn the seventh inning of the Rays\u2019 6-2 win over the Athletics at Tropicana Field, Kiermaier showed off his Platinum Glove defense in the top half, and then followed it up by showing off his power at the plate in the bottom half.</p><p>  \n\n  \n\nDefensively, Kiermaier tracked down a Jurickson Profar liner that looked like it was ticketed for the left-center-field gap. Kiermaier got a good jump on the ball, hit top speed, and then made a leaping play as he got closer to the wall to end the inning. Offensively, Kiermaier connected on a 416-foot, two-run home run to straightaway center field off A\u2019s reliever Yusmeiro Petit to give the Rays a 4-0 lead.\n\n\u2022 [Box score](https://www.mlb.com/gameday/566695/final/box \"undefined\")\n\nWhat felt better for Kiermaier? The catch or the home run?\n\n\u201cI think I will always make more catches than homers that I\u2019ll hit, so I will say the homer,\u201d Kiermaier laughed. \u201cFelt good to barrel one up right there, so I\u2019ll go with the homer.\u201d\n\n  \n\n  \n\n  \n\nThere\u2019s no secret that the Rays are a better team when Kiermaier can pair some offensive production with his stellar defensive play. Over his last 14 games, Kiermaier has three homers and 10 RBIs. The Rays are 9-5 over that span and improved to 6-2 in games where Kiermaier has hit a home run.\n\nKiermaier\u2019s two-run blast and Brandon Lowe\u2019s team-leading 14th home run of the season were enough run support for Rays starter Charlie Morton, who improved to 8-0 this season and lowered his season ERA to 2.10 after another impressive start in his first season with Tampa Bay.\n\n\u201cHe\u2019s been huge,\u201d said Rays manager Kevin Cash, when asked about Morton\u2019s impact this season. \u201cEspecially with Tyler \\[Glasnow\\] going down. He can only pitch once every fifth day, but what he\u2019s provided has been really, really impressive.\u201d</p><p>  \n\n  \n\nMorton struggled with his command early on in the game, but was still able to get through seven scoreless innings and allowed just two base hits. The Rays right-hander ran into some trouble in the third inning, but was able to escape a bases-loaded jam by striking out Khris Davis on three consecutive curveballs and getting Stephen Piscotty to ground out to first base on a 95-mph fastball after mixing in a pair of curveballs.\n\n  \n\n  \n\n\u201cI don\u2019t really feel a ton of pressure,\u201d Morton said. \u201cWhat I do feel pressure with is leaving a cookie over the plate and him driving in three or four runs right there. That\u2019s a problem. Misses, I mean that stuff is going to happen, those innings are going to happen.\n\n  \n\n  \n\n\u201cI would rather get beat with my best stuff. A lot of people would tell you that. I feel good about what we did and how we mixed it in those situations.\u201d\n\n  \n\n  \n\nThat\u2019s the kind of poise that has been infectious throughout the Rays clubhouse this season. Kiermaier said that the team \u201ccouldn\u2019t have had a better pickup\u201d than the two-year, $30 million deal the club inked Morton to over the offseason.\n\n  \n\n  \n\nWith Morton winning his eighth consecutive decision as a member of the Rays, he tied Matt Moore\u2019s franchise record in 2013 for the longest such streak in a season. His 14-start unbeaten streak passes James Shields in '07 for the longest to start a season in club history.\n\n  \n\n  \n\n\u201cCharlie Morton inspires me to make that catch,\u201d Kiermaier said. \u201cThe way Charlie Morton has been going for us all year, the spark and the dominance he has brought to the table, I wanted to make that play for him right there.\u201d\n\n  \n\n  \n\nAt 41-24, the Rays are now a season-high 17 games over .500. They are back atop the American League East, currently holding a half-game lead over the Yankees, who were rained out on Monday, in the division.\n\n  \n\n  \n\n\u201cI think everyone here knows that \\[the Yankees\\] got rained out,\u201d Lowe said. \u201cBut we know that the Yankees are right there, the Red Sox are right there, so it\u2019s not just ours. We\u2019re still fighting to \\[stay in first place\\] and we know people are chomping at our tails to try and get in first place.\u201d</p>",

But he has shown some promise as he has been less pull-happy while producing a .920 OPS over his last 50 plate appearances against right-handed pitchers, dating to May 23.  \n\n\u201cI\u2019m feeling great,\u201d Albies said. \u201cI\u2019m working hard, seeing the ball well and just trying to hit everything up the middle.\u201d  \n\n<b>Acuna\u2019s slam</b><br>\n\nAcuna isn\u2019t nearly as hot as Freeman, who has hit 11 of his 18 home runs while producing a 1.142 OPS over his past 23 games. But last year\u2019s NL Rookie of the Year Award winner might be in the early stages of his own tear. He has homered four times within his past 25 at-bats and he has produced a .967 OPS over his past 10 games.</p><p>  \n\nAcuna\u2019s second-inning grand slam off Pirates reliever Alex McRae wasn\u2019t nearly as energizing as the slam he hit off Dodgers right-hander Walker Buehler in the 2018 NL Division Series. But it put him in the company of greatness. He now has 41 home runs, which moves him past Hank Aaron for the fourth-most homers by a Braves hitter before his 22nd birthday. Eddie Mathews holds the record with 72.</p>",

									"body" : "<p>CHICAGO -- The Nationals kept on rolling Monday night, scoring in six innings, including a six-run ninth, to pummel the White Sox, 12-1, at Guranteed Rate Field. Washington has now won 12 out of 16 games thanks to a red-hot offense, another dominant starting-pitching performance (six-plus innings of one-run ball from Anibal Sanchez) and just enough from its bullpen to hold it all together.\n\nHere\u2019s a few takeaways from Monday\u2019s win:\n\n**Turner starting to heat up**\n\nIn recent days, Nationals manager Dave Martinez pointed out that he had started to see <forge-entity title=\"Trea Turner\" slug=\"trea-turner-607208\" code=\"player\">Trea Turner</forge-entity>\u2019s power stroke start to return. It was Turner who mashed the hardest-hit and longest home run when the Nationals erupted for four consecutive homers on Sunday in San Diego, an encouraging sign for a player who had missed more than a month with a broken right index finger.\n\n\u2022 [Box score](https://www.mlb.com/gameday/567295/final/box \"undefined\")\n\nAnd Turner continued that power surge Monday night, setting the tone for the Nationals offensive outburst. He collected three hits -- a triple to start the third inning, a homer in the fifth and an RBI double to cap an 11-pitch at-bat in the seventh inning -- and just missing a bid for his second career cycle, as he struck out looking and popped out to second base in his final two at-bats.\n\n\u201cAfter missing seven weeks and not playing game speed, it takes a little bit to catch up,\u201d Martinez said. \u201cI think now you\u2019re starting to see Trea play the way he\u2019s capable of playing.\u201d</p><p>While Turner has insisted his injury did not hinder his ability to drive the ball, there\u2019s no doubt he has seen an uptick in power recently. In his first 15 games following the injury, Turner was 17-for-71 at the plate (.254) without a home run, four doubles and a triple. In the eight games since, he has gone 11-for-34 (.324) with three homers, six doubles and a triple. He has a double in four straight games, as well, and has seen his batting average rise from .255 to .284 in that span.\n\n\u201cI just feel like I'm in a little bit more consistent spot right now,\u201d Turner said. \u201cGiving myself a chance to hit multiple pitches in the zone. I feel like I\u2019m not chasing and just kind of commanding the zone for the most part. For me, that's the difference in good hitters and bad hitters. If you can stay in the zone and make them throw you pitches, you'll be able to drive the ball a little bit better.\u201d</p><p>Adam Eaton also had three hits for the Nationals, while Kurt Suzuki capped a five-RBI game with a grand slam in Washington's six-run ninth inning.</p><p>The Nationals' big ninth inning meant Turner got a second chance to complete the cycle. It looked like his night at the plate was over after striking out looking to end the top of the eighth, but Turner got another shot in the final frame, only to popout to the second baseman and end the Nationals' night at the plate.</p><p>**Rosenthal returns to the mound**\n\nIt had been more than a month since Trevor Rosenthal pitched in a big league game, after a five-week process of rebuilding his mechanics in the Minors and working to regain the confidence from a disastrous start to the season. So his scoreless ninth inning on Monday night can be seen as an encouraging building block.\n\nNo, Rosenthal was not perfect. He walked the leadoff man, Jose Rondon, on four pitches. He threw just one of his seven fastballs for a strike. He needed the help of a diving play by Turner to start a double play to escape the inning unscatched. Still, Monday night was the first scoreless appearance of the season for Rosenthal during which he recorded at least one out.\n\n\u201cI\u2019ve been looking forward to getting back out there,\u201d Rosenthal said. \u201cHopefully this is a stepping stone to keep building on for the rest of the season. Hopefully I can just continue to help this team win.\u201d\n\nMartinez had been looking for a way to get Rosenthal into a game after he was activated from the injured list on Saturday, not wanting him to sit for too long and lose the positive steps he took during his rehab assignment. And he saw a few positives from his outing in this game.\n\nRosenthal was able to spot his slider in the strike zone consistently, as five of the six went for strikes, and he was able to regroup after the leadoff walk that threatened to derail his outing.\n\n\u201cI really believe that having an outing like this, and knowing that he can throw his slider, he threw his fastball for a strike at 97, it will definitely help him,\u201d Martinez said. \u201cAnd the more he gets out there, and the more comfortable he gets, and he\u2019s done it \u2026 this guy has been an unbelievable closer for a lot of years, and we just got to keep him on track.\u201d\n\n**Adams suffers left oblique strain**\n\nMatt Adams left the game following his at-bat in the sixth inning after he strained his left oblique during a checked swing. Adams finished the at-bat and popped out to short, but he did not take the field for the bottom of the inning.\n\nThe Nationals will re-evaluate Adams on Tuesday, and while Martinez did not commit to a stint on the injured list, he admitted he was \u201ca little concerned.\u201d\n\n\u201cWhenever it\u2019s an oblique, that\u2019s going to be days missed,\u201d Martinez said.</p>",

It was the type of game for which the Rockies signed <forge-entity title=\"Daniel Murphy\" slug=\"daniel-murphy-563547\" code=\"player\">Daniel Murphy</forge-entity>.\n\nIt was Murphy\u2019s eighth-inning double that set up Ryan McMahon\u2019s tiebreaking single, the difference in the Rockies\u2019 much-needed 6-5 victory over the Cubs, whose loud legion of fans had to watch the people in purple party.\n\n\u2022 [Box score](https://www.mlb.com/gameday/565445/final/box)\n\n\u201cThe atmosphere was great,\u201d said Murphy, who was with the Cubs last October when the Rockies beat them in the National League Wild Card Game in 13 innings at Wrigley Field, 2-1. \u201cThe fans were unbelievable. I\u2019ve experienced Chicago and how they travel on the road. It kind of startled me a bit when I was there. Even this was pretty impressive.\n\n\u201cBut the atmosphere was great, and it was a fun game to play.\u201d</p><p>  \n\nEven though it was June 10, it was a big game to win.\n\nThe Rockies (34-31) had just returned after going 2-4 on the road against the Mets and Cubs, and seemed in need of getting back on the roll that pushed them above .500 during their last homestand.\n\n\u201cAnytime you have a game like this, it breeds confidence, no doubt about it,\u201d Rockies manager Bud Black said. \u201cWe just played these guys last week, some good games in Chicago. Anytime you play a team like this in this atmosphere, it can really give you some momentum.\u201d\n\nAnd Murphy, signed for two years and $24 million, arrived with a catalog of clutch performances -- especially in postseasons with the Mets and during last year\u2019s stretch run with the Cubs -- and the ability to influence others. And while he wasn\u2019t involved in a home run show that included Ian Desmond hitting the longest in MLB this season at 486 feet in the seventh inning, Murphy went 2-for-4 while giving the Rockies the savvy they needed.\n\n\u2022 [Desmond crushes MLB-longest 486-foot homer](https://www.mlb.com/rockies/news/ian-desmond-hits-longest-home-run-of-2019 \"undefined\")</p><p>Murphy had a seven-game RBIs streak snapped Saturday, but he has been a key member of an offense finding its form. In his last 19 games, Murphy is 24-for-70 (.343) with six runs, five doubles, a triple, three home runs and 18 RBIs.\n\nBut when he came up with one out in the eighth against Cubs righty Steve Cishek, Murphy was thinking of one of the at-bats that didn\u2019t go well. In the ninth inning of Rockies\u2019 9-8 loss at Wrigley, Cishek zipped a 2-2 pitch by him. Or as Murphy said, \u201cHe kind of chewed me up and spit me out.\u201d\n\nHe added, \u201cI was just trying to have a better at-bat and, in a perfect world, hit a double. That\u2019s my goal.\u201d\n\nMurphy, not known for speed, stole third on the third pitch of Raimel Tapia\u2019s looking strikeout (he wanted to go earlier). McMahon then lined a 2-1 slider into the right-center gap.\n\n\u201cMurphy is a professional hitter,\u201d McMahon said. \u201cHe stole that bag, was causing a little havoc. Cishek was thinking a little bit about him at third, probably afraid to bounce something, wanting to be a little more perfect with his pitches. [That] got me something to hit.\u201d\n\nCould that have been McMahon following Murphy\u2019s example?\n\n\u201cThe cool thing you get to see is the more times that he gets in that situation, the more times he can pull from previous experiences,\u201d Murphy said. \u201cThat\u2019s what you see -- being able to slow the at-bat down, pick out a pitch and be able to put a good move on it.\u201d</p>",

									"body" : "<p>ANAHEIM -- Rookie right-hander Griffin Canning laid the groundwork with a strong outing, <forge-entity title=\"Mike Trout\" slug=\"mike-trout-545361\" code=\"player\">Mike Trout</forge-entity> tied it with a clutch two-run blast in the seventh and the Angels made the most of a wild eighth inning in a 5-3 win over the Dodgers on Monday in front of a festive crowd of 45,477, which was the largest at Angel Stadium since it was renovated in 1998.\n\n\u201cIt was a big win for us,\u201d Trout said. \u201cThe atmosphere was unbelievable. That\u2019s the best the atmosphere has been all year. Whenever we play the Dodgers here or in L.A. it\u2019s just fun. The competition is real. It\u2019s fun to be a part of.\u201d</p><p>  \n\nHere\u2019s a look at the two-run eighth, Trout\u2019s game-tying blast and Canning\u2019s impressive effort in the victory:\n\n**Angels take the lead without a hit**\n\nThe Angels scored twice in the eighth against Joe Kelly, who was erratic with three walks, two wild pitches and a throwing error to first base. Pinch-hitter <forge-entity title=\"Shohei Ohtani\" slug=\"shohei-ohtani-660271\" code=\"player\">Shohei Ohtani</forge-entity> drew a four-pitch walk to open the inning and it was a sign of things to come.\n\nAfter an error on a pickoff throw from Kelly, Ohtani went to second and Brian Goodwin was intentionally walked. Jonathan Lucroy then walked to load the bases with one out for Wilfredo Tovar. Tovar hit a slow grounder to third and Max Muncy threw home, but it was too late with Russell Martin jumping to catch the throw. After a review, the call on the field stood and Ohtani was safe at home.</p><p>  \n\n\u201cIt's a tough play,\u201d Angels manager Brad Ausmus said. \u201cMuncy fielded it at third and it was an off-balance throw and Russ had to go up to get it. Shohei can run. That's the best secret about him. He's an excellent runner. It looked like they got the call right.\u201d\n\nJust two pitchers later, Kelly threw his second wild pitch to allow a second run to score. It spoiled another strong showing from Dodgers lefty Hyun Jin-Ryu, who limited the Angels to one run over six innings with Kole Calhoun connecting on a solo shot in the second.\n\n\u201cIt can't get any more bizarre,\" said Kelly, who has struggled in his first year with the Dodgers. \"I guess that's average for right now.\"</p><p> \u2022 [Box score](https://www.mlb.com/gameday/564769/final/box \"undefined\")\n</p><p>**Trout comes up huge**\n\nThe Angels appeared headed toward a tough defeat despite Canning\u2019s solid effort, but Trout changed it all with one swing with two outs in the seventh. Trout was 5-for-5 with two homers in his career against Ross Stripling, so the Dodgers brought in reliever Dylan Floro to face him. But it didn't stop Trout from jumping all over a 2-2 slider from Floro and crushing it a projected 402 feet to left to tie the game.\n\n\u201cI was trying to get a pitch I could hit and put the barrel to it, and it went out,\u201d Trout said. \u201cObviously it was a big spot in the game.\u201d</p><p>  \n\n  \n\n**Canning passes stern test**\n\nCanning, making his eighth career start, was tasked with facing a division-leading team for the first time in his young career and gave up three runs on five hits over six innings with five strikeouts. Notably, he registered 18 swings and misses, which was the fourth-highest total against the high-powered Dodgers offense this year. Only Patrick Corbin, Noah Syndergaard and Robbie Ray induced more.\n\nCanning, though, was hurt by a three-run second inning sparked by a one-out double from Corey Seager. With two outs, Canning threw a first-pitch strike to Martin but then hit him with a fastball to put two runners on. Chris Taylor made him pay with a two-run double to left and Kik\u00e9 Hernandez followed with an RBI double that popped out of left fielder Cesar Puello\u2019s glove as he hit the grass on his diving attempt.\n\n\u201cIt wasn\u2019t anything crazy,\u201d Canning said. \u201cJust a few bad pitches that they capitalized there. They\u2019re a really good hitting team. They get paid a lot of money to hit mistakes, so they did that. Just stayed aggressive, didn\u2019t want to back off and just stayed within myself.\u201d\n\nCanning settled down from there, retiring 10 of 11 before running into trouble again in the sixth after surrendering back-to-back singles to open the frame. This time, Canning escaped the jam, striking out Seager and getting Alex Verdugo to pop up before striking out Martin on a 95.6 mph fastball that was his second-hardest pitch of the night despite being his 88th and final offering.</p><p>  \n\n\u201cHe was outstanding,\u201d Ausmus said. \u201cHe continues to be unintimidated by big league lineups, including a very good Dodger lineup. He dug himself out of a little bit of a hole there in the sixth. If he doesn't dig out there, I'm don't know what happens in that game. I'm not sure we win it.\"</p>",
